Local News

Our Country's Delegation to Siam Returns, Arriving in Shanghai Yesterday Morning. Siamese Authorities' Attitude Cordial and Sincere, Overseas Chinese Enthusiastically Support the Central Government, Rich Collection of Materials Awaits Sorting. 98

Our country's delegation to Siam, a group of seven, led by head of delegation Ling Bing and Lin Kanghou, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 6:00 AM aboard the French mail ship Aramis. They issued a written statement detailing the inspection process. Numerous representatives from various groups in Shanghai went to welcome them. A banquet was held last night to welcome them. The details are as follows:

Arriving in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

The Aramis berthed at 5:00 AM yesterday morning. Representatives from various groups went to welcome them in succession. Welcome flags were hung everywhere on the pier, and the atmosphere was quite enthusiastic. Those who arrived included Central Committee member Chu Minyi, Zhou Jue, director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office, Zhao Tiezhang, deputy director, Wu Wentian, section chief of the Ministry of Industry's Labor Department, Liu Yunfang, secretary of the Municipal Council, Wu Yunzhai of the Bankers' Association, Zhang Peishen, Gu Chengan, Gu Huaibing of the National Federation of Commerce, Zhu Boyuan of the Municipal Higher Association, Wang Zhisheng of the China Industrial Federation, Chen Chengzhi of the Aviation Association, Pan Yangyao of the National Products Sales Association, Tao Leqin of the Taxpaying Chinese Association, representatives from the Civic United Association, the Chinese Red Cross, Jinan University, the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, local associations, and relatives of the delegation members, totaling over a hundred people.

Delegation Members Arriving in Shanghai

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office negotiated with customs authorities, and all luggage was exempted from inspection. After the delegation members exchanged greetings with the welcomers, those who were not residing in Shanghai went to the New Asia Hotel to rest. The delegation members who arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning included Ling Bing, head of the delegation, Lin Kanghou, deputy head of the delegation, Wang Zhixin, Ma Chaoyong, Liu Yiling, secretary, Xiong Dansun, and Ye Xiangfa, totaling seven people. Two delegation members, Liu Hou and Cao Yumin, remained in Saigon for inspection. Delegation member Yu Ming returned to his native Guangdong province to visit relatives. Others, such as Li Gan, Fang Zhizhen, Huang Tianjue, Yang Donglin, and Chen Chongkan, returned to the country earlier. The delegation plans to stay in Shanghai for one day and will return to the capital today to report on their mission.

Sorting Materials

The delegation brought back gifts from the Siamese authorities and overseas Chinese, numbering about seventy boxes, demonstrating the cordiality of Sino-Siamese relations and the deep love of the overseas Chinese. All the inspection materials will be compiled by the relevant delegation members, with a two-month period set aside for sorting after returning to the country. The content is divided into overseas Chinese affairs, economy, education, diplomacy, commerce, etc. In the future, in addition to reporting to the competent authorities, they will also be compiled into a book to report to the government. Regarding the development of Sino-Siamese commerce, according to delegation head Ling, they exchanged opinions with the authorities there several times, and the results were very good. Siam also hopes to work with our country to promote commerce. As for specific measures, they will be discussed after reporting to the government.

Written Statement

The delegation issued a written statement saying, "Our delegation's trip to Siam began preparations in the autumn of last year. Due to various reasons, the departure date was delayed several times. It was not until May 26 of this year that we departed from Shanghai on the Italian mail ship Victoria, passing through Hong Kong, Manila, Singapore, Penang, and other places. On June 6, we arrived in Bangkok, the capital of Siam, and stayed in Siam for a little over a month. At the beginning of July, we returned via Penang to Singapore and took the French mail ship Aramis back to the country via Saigon. Today, we arrived safely in Shanghai, deeply grateful for the concern and care of those who care about our delegation and friends from all walks of life. Now, we will describe the course of this trip and the impressions we have gained, as follows: The important task of our delegation is to connect national relations, comfort overseas Chinese, and at the same time inspect various undertakings in Siam. The reason is that in the summer of last year, the representatives of the Siamese People's Council had an organization for a Far East inspection tour to our country. Our government and people thought that reciprocity was a necessary etiquette between nations, so we organized this delegation to go and reciprocate. For nearly a hundred years, there have been no formal national relations between China and Siam. Neither side has established embassies or consulates. This is also an opportunity to allow the more than two million overseas Chinese in Siam to understand the current situation of the motherland and the necessity of government attention. Siam is located between French Indochina and British Burma, with a territorial area of approximately 200,000 square miles and a population of over 11 million. Among them, one-quarter are purely Siamese, one-quarter are purely overseas Chinese, and the rest, except for a small number of foreigners, are mixed Chinese-Siamese. This shows the deep relationship between China and Siam. This kind of special situation is rare in the world. Siam's products are mainly rice and wood. There are also many other products such as leather, catalpa, rubber, and tin. Among them, rice accounts for about half of the annual direct sales to Hong Kong and the interior of our country. The rest is mostly sold to British Malaya and the Dutch East Indies, etc. In the final analysis, it is also consumed by the overseas Chinese in the above-mentioned places. Therefore, China and Siam not only have a very deep relationship in blood, but also have an inseparable trend in economy. Since Siam changed its government, the government authorities have been working hard to govern the country, and all measures have far-reaching plans, and all kinds of government affairs can be smoothly implemented, and the people are also full of vigor and vitality, and the future development is still promising. What is especially admirable is the spirit of the ruling authorities to strive for the country peacefully and their open and upright attitude. All discussions are extremely sincere and cordial. Although there have been no formal national relations between China and Siam in the past, the efforts of our ancestors over hundreds of years have made the national feelings harmonious, as close as brothers and sisters, not comparable to casual friends. Therefore, my colleagues' talks with the Prime Minister, Foreign Affairs, Economy, Agriculture, Education, and other relevant ministers are as direct as family members talking about family affairs, without adhering to customary etiquette. As for the results of the discussions, they still need to be formally reported to the government, and it is not yet time to release them. We cannot talk more about it at this time. What can be gratifying is that the delegation's trip has not failed its mission. Not only the goodwill of the Siamese government and people, but also the delegation's return, brings the goodwill of the Siamese government and people with it. Regarding comforting overseas Chinese, the delegation was instructed by President Chiang to convey his regards. After arriving in Siam, my colleagues went to various places to promote the domestic situation. Fortunately, the central government's prestige was deeply welcomed by the overseas Chinese. However, overseas Chinese in various places have not had envoys coming and going between the two countries for a long time. This trip by the delegation is the only one in nearly a hundred years. As a result, people along the north-south railway came out to meet them, young and old, just to see my colleagues, even waiting late at night, giving many treasures. The original intention of my colleagues was to comfort, but in the end, we troubled the overseas Chinese, which is very disturbing. However, it can also be seen that the overseas Chinese support the central government enthusiastically. As for the scope of inspection, it is very broad, especially focusing on internal affairs, diplomacy, education, and economic construction. Although the time is short and the manpower is limited, the collected materials are still rich. After sorting them out and reporting them to the government, we will select the best ones to publish to inform those who care about the delegation and to correct people from all walks of life."

Public Banquet Last Night

The National Federation of Commerce, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Taxpaying Chinese Association, the Local Association, the Civic United Association of the First Special District, the Bankers' Association, the Aviation Association, the International Trade Association, and other twenty-nine public groups, held a public banquet for the delegation to Siam at the Bankers' Association Club on Hong Kong Road at 7:00 PM last night. Head of delegation Ling Bing, Deputy Head Lin Kanghou, and delegates from the delegation's secretariat and various public groups, including Hu Xiyuan, Yuan Ludeng, Wang Xiaoji, Wu Yunzhu, Du Yuesheng, Huang Renzhi, Zhou Xuexiang, Wang Zhisheng, Pan Yangyao, Xu Xiaochu, Wang Manyun, Liu Shenying, Fang Yixian, and others, totaling over seventy people, attended. As the wine reached its peak, Chairman Wang Xiaoji stood up and gave a welcome speech, saying, "Today we welcome the delegation to Siam back to the country. This morning, representatives from public groups all went to the pier to welcome them, but still felt that it was not enough. Therefore, we have prepared a small amount of wine to cleanse the dust for the delegation and to express our respect. During the delegation's trip abroad, the domestic political situation changed. I believe that the delegation must have been very worried. Fortunately, the situation turned out very well, and the country has the hope of unification as a result. It can be said that we were afraid and happy at the same time. The delegation has worked hard for the country in the hot summer, which makes us admire them very much. Now, we invite the two delegation heads, Ling and Lin, to report on the inspection process." Amidst applause, head of delegation Ling gave a speech, saying, "Chairman, representatives, today we are very grateful for the enthusiastic reception from the public groups in Shanghai. The most important missions of our delegation's inspection in Siam are two: First, to connect national relations. China and Siam have had almost no national relations for nearly a hundred years. Neither side has sent envoys or consulates. Therefore, we felt very apprehensive when we set off, wondering whether the Siamese government would welcome us or not, and whether they were sincere. After arriving there, the Siamese government authorities were very sincere to us. After talking with them, we felt that the previous rumors about the Siamese government were too exaggerated. Another point that deserves our attention is that Siam is an emerging country. The responsible persons in the government are mostly ambitious young people. Although they may lack experience, they are full of vigor and have unlimited hope for the future. As for the national relations between China and Siam, from the perspective of race and economy, there is a natural alliance. In the future, if we send envoys and consulates to each other and treat each other with sincerity and goodwill, we will be brothers. Second, to comfort overseas Chinese. This trip by our delegation to Siam is the first time in nearly a hundred years that the government has officially sent representatives there. Therefore, the local overseas Chinese welcomed our delegation wholeheartedly, eager to see my colleagues. It can also be seen that although the overseas Chinese have been abroad for a long time, they still care very much about the motherland and protect the country. However, there is a weakness among the overseas Chinese, that is, they do not communicate with each other. Their group organizations are not sound, their will cannot be unified, and they even split into different factions and attack each other. This is the fatal wound of the overseas Chinese' future. Wherever our delegation went, we earnestly advised them to unite with each other and told them about all the current facilities of the domestic government to strengthen their feelings for the motherland," and so on. Deputy head of delegation Lin Kanghou gave a speech, saying, "The delegation is jointly organized by officials and businessmen, starting with this one. Head of delegation Ling is an official, and I, as the deputy head, am a businessman. This inspection in Siam is not only a discussion between officials and businessmen, but also a division of labor and cooperation. All the inspection processes are being compiled into reports, which will be reported to the government first, and may be published publicly in the future. What I want to say to the representatives now are four feelings that arose after the inspection, which can also be said to be four hopes: (1) The fatal wound of the overseas Chinese, as head of delegation Ling just said, is their inability to communicate with each other. Therefore, the first hope is that the overseas Chinese can unite; (2) The older overseas Chinese in Siam mostly only speak dialects, while the younger people can speak Mandarin and have more advanced ideas. Therefore, we advise the overseas Chinese to set up more schools and promote education; (3) Most of the overseas Chinese in Siam are from Guangdong and Fujian provinces, but they inevitably have gaps after living in foreign lands for a long time. Therefore, we hope that they will also return to the country to take a look; (4) The promotion of national products in Siam is difficult because there are no formal national relations. For example, the same goods are suppressed due to different tax rates. Although there is a chamber of commerce in Siam, it has not been able to show its strength. In short, if we want to promote national products in Southeast Asia, the government must come forward to preside over it. I hope that head of delegation Ling can suggest this to the government after returning to the capital." The guests and hosts dispersed happily at about 9:00 PM.

Group Photo After the Delegation to Siam Returned to Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Municipal Chamber of Commerce's Investigation and Reply: The Accumulation Loan Silver Company Is As Such, Changed from Japanese to Portuguese Capital, Unable to Investigate Whether There Is Capital or Not 99

The New Sound Society says that the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce was ordered by the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to investigate and report in detail the internal situation of the Shanghai Citizens' Accumulation Loan Silver Company. The chamber has sent people to investigate and found that the Shanghai Citizens' Accumulation Loan Silver Company is located at No. 150 Guangdong Road. It was opened in May of this year. Initially, it was nominally a Japanese company, but in June it was changed to a Portuguese company. The company name was also changed to Shanghai Accumulation Loan Silver Company. The general manager is the Portuguese Remidice, and the Chinese manager is Zhou Shutang. Its business specializes in collecting money from the lower and middle classes, called the Public Savings Standard Society. According to Zhou, the company is registered with the Portuguese Consulate and has about two hundred members, mostly Class A members. The company's profits are seven yuan per month for each of the Class A and B groups, and fifteen yuan per month for the Class C group. It is currently in a trial period and has not yet officially opened. When asked how much capital it has and whether it is a Sino-foreign joint venture, he was tight-lipped. Observing the company's situation, it has just been opened, but the nationality name has been changed. Examining the license given by the Portuguese Consulate, there are signs of tampering. It seems to be mixed with another company's license. The existence of Japanese capital cannot be investigated. It is said that the chamber has reported it to the Social Affairs Bureau.

Three Groups, Including the All-Zhejiang Public Association, Welcome Chairman Bai Jiansheng. Moving East to Govern Zhejiang Province, the People of Zhejiang Are Looking Forward to It Like Looking at Clouds and Rainbows. 100

The Datong News Agency says that three groups in Shanghai, including the All-Zhejiang Public Association, the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association, and the Shaoxing Seven Counties Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association, jointly sent a telegram to welcome Bai Chongxi to move east to govern Zhejiang. The original telegram said, "To Mr. Bai Jiansheng of Nanning, hearing that you are moving east, those who can govern Guangxi can govern Zhejiang. We are looking forward to it like looking at clouds and rainbows. We respectfully welcome you. Please consider it. Shanghai All-Zhejiang Public Association, Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association, Shaoxing Seven Counties Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association kowtow."

Osdoman Talks About Sino-Iranian Relations 101

And the Trade Status of the Two Countries

The New Sound Society says that since the Iranian state (i.e., Persia) upgraded its consulate in Shanghai to a consulate general and took charge of foreign affairs, it has been striving to strengthen Sino-Iranian relations. Now, the Iranian Consul General Osdoman will be transferred back to his country in accordance with the regulations of the Iranian Ministry of Foreign Affairs. A reporter from the New Sound Society visited Mr. Osdoman at the consulate general and received the following interview:

Returning Home as Usual

Mr. Osdoman first said, "The regulations of our Ministry of Foreign Affairs are roughly similar to those of your country. Diplomats abroad cannot serve for more than five years. Those who have stayed abroad for five years should return to Tehran (the Iranian capital) to work in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for one year in order to understand the domestic and foreign diplomatic situation before taking up posts in other countries." Mr. Osdoman also said that he had served as a consul in India for three years, and then came to Shanghai to establish a consulate, which was promoted to the first consul general in February of this year. He has been stationed in China for almost two years. He is about to return home soon. His successor as consul general will leave Iran for Shanghai soon. In order to further strengthen contact with our country and intensify work, the Iranian Ministry of Foreign Affairs has specially dispatched a secretary to Shanghai to assist the affairs of the Consulate General.

Setting Up a Bureau in This City

The Iranian Ministry of Economy has three departments: Commerce, Industry, and Agriculture. The Commerce Department plans to set up trade bureaus in Europe, America, and Asia to facilitate increased foreign trade. In addition to setting up one bureau in Europe and America each, two special bureaus will be set up in Asia. One of the Asian bureaus has already established a general office in Mumbai. The bureau includes Iran's trade with India, China, Japan, and other countries. The Ministry of Economy has specially appointed Mr. Oweysi, an important official of the ministry, to be in charge of Far East trade. Mr. Oweysi is entrusted with the mission of representing the Iranian Imperial Government's commercial commissioner. He will come to Shanghai soon to handle trade with China and will establish a trade bureau in this city.

Handling Trade

Mr. Osdoman also talked about trade between China and Iran, saying that the goods that Iran transports to our country for sale should be mainly cotton, wool, cigarettes, dried fruits, wines, iron, acids, and flour. It is said that buyers have been found for iron acids and flour, and the goods will be transported to Shanghai soon. The goods that our country transports to Iran should be mainly silk and tea (these two items have long been important trades between China and Iran), porcelain, embroidery, and other luxury goods. Mr. Osdoman finally said that China is now tending towards true unification under the leadership of General Chiang, and there will definitely be new developments in everything. He hopes that China will also establish a trade bureau in Iran in order to further enrich the commercial friendship between the two countries.

The Yangtze River Water Recedes. This Year, We Can Avoid Floods. Farmland Along the River and Lakes Are Ripe. 103

In previous years, at this time, the Yangtze River water level between Hankou and Xunyang was at least forty-seven or forty-eight feet. The farmland along the river often suffered from flooding. Because the river rose and the beaches were submerged, the route along the shallow banks of the river was unclear for ships sailing upstream and downstream, often mistakenly entering farmland. The Taikoo Anqing Wheel's accident last year was due to this reason. Therefore, during the flood season, the Yangtze River navigation industry is always wary. Mr. Chen Yukun, owner of the China Merchants Bureau's Jiangshun steamboat, said to reporters after returning to Shanghai from Hankou yesterday that the upper reaches of the Yangtze River this year have reversed the usual summer pattern of previous years. The water level in Hankou and Jiujiang has been decreasing day by day, with the maximum being less than twenty-nine feet, a decrease of about twenty feet compared to last year. The water in Dongting Lake has also decreased, and the farmland in more than twenty counties around the lake is celebrating a bumper harvest. The farmland along the river in Anhui and Jiangxi provinces has also had a large harvest of rice and grains due to the shallower water, which is rare in the past twenty years. Because the water in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River has decreased, the upstream and downstream ships have been spared from going the wrong way or running aground. From this, we can infer that the Yangtze River area can avoid floods this year. However, the Qingtianshi section of the Yangtze River near Tongzhou has only twenty to fourteen feet of water at the deepest point due to the low river level. The sandy beaches are interspersed, causing all the heavy-laden ships to run aground, making navigation very difficult.

Page 11

National Sugar Production and Sales Association to Be Established Next Month on the First; Inaugural Board Meeting Held Yesterday, Elected Feng Rui as Chairman 104

For the sake of improving sugar quality, increasing sugar production, and promoting sales, national sugar manufacturers have formed the China National Sugar Production and Sales Association. A meeting of initiators was held recently, drafting articles of association and electing directors. After submitting to the relevant ministry for approval, the inaugural board meeting was held yesterday. Feng Rui was elected as chairman, Huang Jiangquan and others as executive directors, and the association's establishment was set for August 1st. Details are as follows:

Election of Directors

Since factories were established in Guangdong and Guangxi provinces to refine sugar using new methods, and Sichuan province is also actively progressing, China's sugar industry has seen improved quality and increased quantity. To consolidate the foundation of the national sugar industry and seek cooperation in production and sales, various manufacturers initiated the establishment of the National Sugar Production and Sales Association. Members include six Guangdong sugar factories, one each from Guangxi and Shandong, and the Sichuan sugar factory preparation office. On the sugar merchant side, there is the Shanghai Sugar Trade Association and its 53 members. A meeting of initiators was held recently, drafting articles of association and electing fourteen directors including Feng Rui. These actions have been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval.

Origin of the Organization

The original text regarding the origin of the association states: "Sugar is one of the necessities of life. Our country's annual sales require 20 million piculs, mostly reliant on foreign sugar in the past five years, resulting in an outflow of no less than 200 million yuan annually. A country's economy is like the lifeblood of a person; constant outflow inevitably leads to depletion. Aware of this, the government has specially increased import tariffs to revive the national sugar industry and prevent the overflow of profit rights. At the same time, it is also the only opportunity for our sugarcane farmers and sugar merchants to revitalize their businesses. In recent years, the national sugar production has been increasing year by year and month by month. Given time, it can become self-sufficient. While national sugar is gradually reviving, the enemy is urgently plotting to destroy us with endless tricks. Recent examples include strengthening smuggling and pressuring for tax reductions. If we do not rise up and resist, the grand plan for the revival of national sugar will inevitably be destroyed, and we will become their prey. At this critical juncture, it is the time for the survival of national sugar. Seize the moment; a slight delay will be lost. Only through painful self-awareness and urgent action can all of our national sugar producers and sellers unite, without distinction, and support each other. Therefore, in response to the needs of the times, this association is specifically organized to use collective strength to seek the development of national sugar, to live up to the government's intention to save the country through production, and to maintain our own interdependent survival. The people's livelihood and the national economy all depend on it."

First Meeting

The elected directors took office yesterday, and the first meeting was held at 3 p.m. at the association's office on Min Guo Road. The directors present were Feng Rui (represented by Lin Yi), Huang Jiangquan, Shen Zhennan (represented by Huang Baoqiu), Yuan Liang (represented by Lin Qunyi), Lu Zuofu (represented by Zhang Shen), Shi Yulin, Zheng Zenan, Zheng Yizhou, Chen Yuren, Yang Wenshao, Jiang Yachen, Lang Guangrui, and Chen Xinfu, a total of fourteen people. The meeting proceeded as scheduled, and Feng Rui was publicly elected as the interim chairman. After delivering a report, it was resolved to elect Feng Rui as chairman, and Huang Jiangquan, Zheng Zenan, Lang Guangrui, Yang Wenshao, Zheng Yizhou, and Chen Yuren as executive directors. It was also resolved to establish three groups under the board of directors: General Affairs, Affairs, and Finance. Lin Qunyi was appointed as the director of General Affairs, Zheng Zenan concurrently as the director of Affairs, and Shi Yulin concurrently as the director of Finance. The inaugural meeting is scheduled for August 1st at the Sugar Trade Association on Fuyou Road in the Nanshi district. An telegram has been sent to Guangdong requesting Feng Rui to come to Shanghai to attend, and invitations have been sent to various sectors to participate in the ceremony. The meeting adjourned at 5 p.m.

Key Points of Association Affairs

The association's articles of association are divided into several chapters, including general principles, objectives, association affairs, organization, membership, and funding. The membership is divided into several types, including sugar factories and sugar merchants. The key points of association affairs are: (A) To handle all matters related to national sugar in order to complete its mission; (B) To investigate the production and sales volume of sugar in various countries around the world, as well as their planting and manufacturing methods; (C) To compile national sugar production and sales statistics and to find ways to adjust supply and demand; (D) To be responsible for investigating the proper transportation of national sugar and to issue certificates and guarantees to facilitate transportation and sales; (E) To guide and improve sugar production methods and to find ways to promote its sales; (F) To provide loans or other relief to sugarcane farmers, manufacturers, and producers when deemed necessary to support their production; (G) Matters concerning the protection of state-owned and private sugar industries; (H) Assisting in the inspection of imported and exported sugar under the entrustment of the government; (I) Other methods for promoting the development of national sugar. The association's headquarters will be located in Shanghai, and branches or offices will be established in important sugar production and sales areas. It is said that organizational regulations and detailed rules of procedure are still being drafted at future meetings.

The Salt Affairs Audit Office Handles the Aftermath Peacefully

Aftermath of the Daishan Salt Riot 111

Following the Daishan salt riot in Zhenhai County, Zhejiang Province, the Salt Affairs Audit Office was very concerned. In addition to immediately sending Zhang Zhong, director of the Tax Police Bureau, to Daishan to investigate, Yu Bingxun was also appointed as the director of the Daishan Weighing and Distribution Bureau and concurrently as the head of the Daishan Salt Field to handle the aftermath. According to a reporter from the China Times News Agency, the incident was caused by a misunderstanding among the salt farmers of Daishan regarding the management of salt piles. The establishment of salt piles was due to the fact that the Daishan salt fields were very disorganized, and management and tax collection were not well-organized. Therefore, it was recently planned to build a salt pile next to each field to facilitate management. On the 13th of this month, surveyors were sent to Daishan to conduct measurements, but the salt farmers, unaware and without asking about the reason, beat and insulted the surveyors. Later, the salt police from the Weighing and Distribution Bureau went to rescue them, leading to a conflict that angered the local salt farmers. More than 2,000 people gathered, carrying new-style firearms, dry firewood, kerosene, and other items, and rushed to the Weighing and Distribution Bureau, setting it on fire. Twelve salt affairs personnel were brutally murdered, their stomachs cut open and filled with stones before being thrown into the sea. The rumor that more than a hundred salt farmers were killed or injured, and that the salt police were harsh on the salt farmers, may not be accurate. The local salt farmers are very fierce, and the salt police fear them like tigers. It is heard that the fish and salt tax in Daishan is only 20 cents per picul, which is vastly different from the Shanghai salt tax of 7.2 yuan per picul. Currently, the Salt Affairs Audit Office is handling the aftermath of the Daishan salt riot by peacefully guiding the Daishan salt farmers and actively reorganizing the local salt fields.

Japanese Textile Mills in Shanghai Buy Up Spindles from Two Factories 112

Japanese merchants are constantly pushing forward with their attempts to expand the raw material market for the textile industry in China. Most of the Chinese-owned textile mills in North China have been bought and reorganized by Japanese merchants to establish a textile industry foundation in northern China, leaving a few Chinese merchants struggling under severe threat from Japanese merchants. A reporter from the Dagon News Agency learned from the Shanghai textile industry yesterday that the Tongchang Textile Mill at the Youche Wharf in Nanshi and the Zhenhua Textile Mill at the end of Lan Road in Yangshupu, which had announced their closure last year due to financial difficulties, each had more than 15,000 spindles. The largest of the Chinese-owned textile mills, the Japanese-owned Naigaiwata Textile Mill, recently bought all the internal machinery and spindles of these two factories. After rearranging and dismantling them, they will be allocated for use within the factory. According to a textile industry magnate, Chinese-owned textile mills are already in dire straits and unable to escape being competed against by the Japanese. If there is no practical way to provide relief, Chinese-owned textile mills will all go bankrupt within two years. He hopes that the authorities will provide substantial assistance during this critical period to help reverse the impending collapse of the industry.

Zhejiang Antimony Mine Officially Opened 113

Qian Xichan and Others Initiated the Organization

Organizing the Jincheng Antimony Mine Company

China has the richest antimony reserves, accounting for about 70% of the world's antimony production. Twenty years ago, the demand for antimony in the British and American metal industries increased daily, and the price of antimony rose from 200 yuan to 1,300 yuan per ton. Those who mined antimony in Hunan earlier were able to obtain huge profits. In recent years, Hunan's antimony production has reached 20,000 to 30,000 tons per year, worth 10 to 30 million yuan. The lives of 300,000 Hunan villagers depend on antimony mining. As a result, antimony in Hunan is not only a major part of Hunan's production but also the most famous antimony-producing area in the world. At the same time, Chinese people have seen the great profits to be made in the antimony industry, and the number of people searching for and mining antimony has gradually increased. Unfortunately, antimony-containing mountains in China are not easy to find, and there are none besides Hunan. For more than a decade, only western Guangdong has had some minor discoveries, but production is very small. In 1934, a very rich antimony mine was discovered at Jingzhou Town in the Huizhou region, on the border of Zhejiang and Anhui provinces. With the approval of the Ministry of Industry, Chinese people used indigenous methods to mine it on a trial basis for two years, confirming that the quality was excellent (above 70 degrees) and the quantity was abundant (above 30 metric tons). This year, foreign technicians were hired to work day and night, and two antimony veins were found successively. The antimony quality is 70 degrees, which is higher than Hunan antimony. However, due to imperfect personnel organization, the 10,000 yuan invested did not yield optimistic results. Now, Qian Xiqiao, a prominent figure in Hangzhou's political circles, has taken the lead in inviting foreign mining experts to continue mining. A fund of 60,000 yuan has been raised to formally establish the Jincheng Antimony Mine Limited Liability Company. Lockman, the inventor of the fire extinguisher, has been hired to provide technical and personnel assistance and to serve as a standing member of the preparatory committee. A business office and transportation office have been established in Shanghai to conduct planned mining. It is expected that a minimum of five tons of goods can be shipped daily in the short term. In that case, in addition to Hunan antimony and Guangdong antimony, there will be Zhejiang antimony for export.

Silk Industry Slump, Tianxing Silk Factory Suspends Operations 121

The Tianxing Silk Weaving Factory in Sanxingfang, Tangshan Road, Hongkou, has been operating for many years. In the past, it was still able to make a profit, so the factory's operations were also developing day by day. Last year, due to the social recession, and this year even more so due to the impact of smuggling in North China, business has declined sharply. It had already reduced workers' wages by 20% in February of last year, but it was still difficult to maintain. On May 20 of this year, it announced a suspension of operations, stating that it was waiting to change the weaving machine patterns before resuming work. However, it has been more than two months and there has been no sign of resumption. Although it has issued two food allowances of five yuan per worker, it has been a long time, making it difficult to maintain a livelihood, and the situation is becoming more difficult. Yesterday, representatives Jiang Lianfang, Sun Sihai, Tan Cao Yi, Jiang Hongshan, and others, prepared documents and submitted them to the Party and government agencies, requesting that the factory be ordered to resume work immediately to maintain livelihoods.

Resolution of the Hongxing Labor Strike: Full Resumption of Work This Morning 122

Following Guidance from the Party Headquarters

Awaiting Mediation of the Dispute

The labor dispute at the Hongxing Hosiery Factory on Caishi Road in the French Concession, which had been ongoing for a month due to the factory's insistence on dismissing the union director, leading to extreme positions on both sides, has remained unresolved and has caused other disturbances. The Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, considering the prolonged Hongxing labor strike to be of great importance to national industry and social stability, summoned Zhang Zhuyun, director of the Second District Knitting Industry Union, and worker representatives Qiu Yixin and Ji Zongxi, for talks yesterday morning. The Party Headquarters earnestly advised the workers to return to work immediately, while the dismissed workers and the workers' proposed wage conditions should await legal processing. The representatives agreed and returned to the union, convening a workers' assembly. The assembly passed a resolution to accept the Municipal Party Headquarters' advice and for all workers to return to the factory to resume work at 5:00 AM this morning. The labor-management dispute will await handling by the Party and government.

Niu Yongjian and Others Plan to Build Ping Shan Park: Commemorating Historical Sites and Inspiring Modern People 125

Niu Yongjian, President of the Examination Yuan, along with local elites Shang Yibangyan, Yan Qi, Zhang Jingye, Niu Changyao, Zhu Hange, and others, are currently planning to build Ping Shan Park between Beiqiao and Yutang. The public notice states: After reading through local gazetteers, although there are many high mountains and lofty ridges in the world, they are all stone or earthen mountains, and there is no mountain named after a bottle except for our Shanghai County. It is said that in the Jin Dynasty, Ping Shan, the Internal History, was originally the village of giants. When Yuan Shan Song, a pirate, captured him, he kept a wine bottle, which accumulated into a mound and became the name. According to the old stele, during the Five Dynasties, Qian Yuqiu was good at leading Sichuan soldiers and ordered his soldiers to carry a tile bottle filled with water to prevent thirst. The army traveled to the village of giants and found a well with extremely sweet and delicious water. The soldiers scrambled to drink, and their bottles became empty and were discarded there, accumulating into a mountain. After the mountain was formed, the well was lost and could not be found. Later, the well was discovered on the bank of the Yutang River, and it was said that this well was moved by heaven. In front of the mountain, there are two ancient ginkgo trees with trunks that can be embraced more than ten times, said to be over a thousand years old. In the past, someone sawed one of them, and when the saw reached about a foot, blood suddenly spurted out, so they stopped. Today, there is still a scar about a foot long, shaped like a pine board patch, and people commonly call it "pine branch patched ginkgo." The stone lions, such as Dujiaoshan Gate, are all famous historical sites. In the past dynasties, grand Taoist temples were built here and were greatly renovated during the Chongzhen reign of the Ming Dynasty and the Qianlong reign of the Qing Dynasty. The pavilions and towers were magnificent for a time. Unfortunately, over hundreds of years, things have changed, and the place has become overgrown with thorns and is about to be abandoned. The Yutang People's Education Center, for research and experimentation, and to calculate the number of people who are disturbed and spend money, together with enthusiastic local people, have established a Ping Shan branch here. Since Shanghai was opened as a port, government buildings have been built densely, roads crisscross, and transportation is convenient. For the establishment of new facilities, we earnestly use the greatest strength. Ping Shan is close to the new county, so build a park here, plant flowers and trees, and equip bathrooms, reading rooms, dormitories, libraries, and clubs separately to guide the opening of a new era. We hope everyone will come to support and witness its completion soon.

Private Purchase of Treasury Bonds, Losses Borne by the Bank: Hua An Bank's Fang Chuanxun Accused of Breach of Trust for the "Wonderful Method" of Personal Gains and Bank Losses 130

Fang Chuanhong (also known as Fang Su'an), a managing director of Hua An Bank (and owner of the An Kang Money Exchange on Houma Road), was sued in the First Special District Local Court by shareholders Ding Zhixian, represented by lawyers Yang Ruinian, on criminal charges of breach of trust. Yesterday afternoon, the judge held a court hearing. According to the plaintiff, Hua An Bank has a total capital of 500,000 yuan, of which he owns ten shares, accounting for a capital of 1,000 yuan. Last summer, when the defendant was the auditor, he purchased 50,000 yuan of customs treasury bonds. Later, seeing the market price fall, he requested the bank's general manager, Ye Jingliang, to approve the transfer of the 50,000 yuan treasury bonds to the bank's purchase, causing the bank to lose 593 yuan, 7 jiao, and 3 fen. The plaintiff accused the defendant of this kind of clever behavior of personal gains and bank losses, which clearly constitutes a breach of trust. Therefore, in order to protect the original capital, he has filed a request for mediation with the civil court. Because the defendant did not attend the mediation, it was unsuccessful. Therefore, he filed a criminal lawsuit. The defendant, Fang Chuanxun, denied that there was a breach of trust. Judge Xiao believed that the civil issue should be resolved first, and then the criminal issue could be addressed, so he immediately ruled to suspend the trial and ordered the plaintiff to first file a civil lawsuit with the civil court to await further action. In addition to Ding Zhixian, Li Shanxiang, another shareholder of Hua An Bank, has also entrusted lawyer Wu Kaisheng to sue Fang for breach of trust in the First Special District Court. It is reported that the trial will be held soon.

South Pacific Hurricane Far from Shanghai: Observatory Denies Distance of Only 600 Nautical Miles 136

Yesterday's newspaper reported that the observatory reported that the hurricane originating near Yabu Island in the South Pacific was only 660 nautical miles from Shanghai. The observatory authorities have denied this, saying that the hurricane is very far from Shanghai and that the reported distance of 660 nautical miles from Shanghai is absolutely unfounded. The distance of the hurricane from Shanghai is very important to maritime affairs, and they deeply regret this unfounded report. As for the direction of the hurricane yesterday, according to the station's report, at 6:00 AM on the 27th, the hurricane had reached the sea area at 130 degrees east longitude and 13 degrees north latitude. The center of the wind was 120 nautical miles, and the wind was moving very slowly, appearing to hover in place. The 4:00 PM report stated that the wind was still hovering in place.

Another Incident of Sparrows' Hunger: Boiling Lily Soup Leads to a Fire: Four Buildings Destroyed in Guilan Lane, Liyuan Road 138

At around 2:30 AM yesterday morning, a sudden fire broke out upstairs at No. 7 Guilan Lane, Liyuan Road, and the flames quickly reached the roof and spread to neighboring houses. The fire was uncontrollable. Fire brigades from various districts rushed to the scene with pump trucks to connect to water and extinguish the fire, which was quickly extinguished. Four buildings, Nos. 7, 6, 8, and 9, were destroyed in the fire. The police station in charge detained the Jiaxing maid Wu Guibao, who was responsible for the fire, and sent her to the Ximen Branch. According to her confession, the hostess was playing mahjong downstairs at the time and suddenly felt hungry, so she asked her to boil lily soup to satisfy her hunger. She lit the kerosene stove and went downstairs. Unexpectedly, the stove burned the bed curtains. When she went upstairs and realized it, the room was already engulfed in flames. She immediately screamed for help and ran out the door, and was arrested. The police were ordered to temporarily detain her and take Wu Guibao to identify and arrest her master and bring them to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Lu Jin Induces Good Women into Prostitution: Sentenced 140

Pan Yuzhen, a woman from Yixing, 19 years old, lived with her brother Pan Yupei and sister-in-law Pan Lu in the countryside. This month, Lu Jin, a woman from Yixing residing at No. 8 Qingyuli, Chongqing Road, returned to her hometown and, knowing Pan and seeing her young and easily deceived, falsely claimed to find a job in a yarn factory for her. On the 13th of this month, Pan Yuzhen and her brother and sister-in-law came to Shanghai together and lodged in Room 25 of the Liangxi Hostel at No. 144 Hubei Road. Unexpectedly, Lu Jin had ulterior motives. While Pan's sister-in-law was asleep, she induced Pan Yuzhen to receive guests and introduced a man to sleep with Pan, earning 1.8 yuan. The next day, she received another guest, earning 2 yuan. All the money was taken by Lu Jin. Later, this mysterious matter was discovered by Pan's brother and sister-in-law, who warned her and moved to a better place. They all lodged at Lu Jin's place. For ten days, Pan and others could not find a job, so they decided to return home by boat the day before yesterday. Unexpectedly, Lu Jin demanded 16 yuan for food and accommodation expenses for the past two weeks. Pan Yupei believed that she had lost all conscience, had induced her sister into prostitution, and now wanted to take the opportunity to extort money, so they quarreled and fought each other. Detectives from No. 183 and No. 967 saw this and brought all 1,000 people to the Chengdu Road Police Station. Detective Chen Yaoting was specially assigned to investigate, and Lu Jin was ordered to be detained. Yesterday, she was sent to the Criminal Division 2 of the Special First Court. Attorney Jiang Baolian of the Police Station prosecuted her according to law. Pan Yuzhen confessed that she had been lured to Shanghai by the defendant Lu Jin and had received guests at the Liangxi Hostel. Lu Jin confessed that the guests received by Pan were not introduced by her and could be investigated. Judge Huang Daxi verified the confession and sentenced Lu Jin to two months of imprisonment for intending to profit and luring a woman from a good family to commit adultery with others. Pan Yuzhen was taken back by her brother and sister-in-law.

Qian Chunlang, a 29-year-old shipowner from Chongming, lives at No. 13 Yaokong Bridge at the end of Tangming Road. Yesterday morning, he went to Pudong for business and was bitten on his left foot by a poisonous snake (commonly known as a gray earth turtle). His foot immediately swelled and he felt unbearable pain. He immediately crossed the river and went home to find a way to treat it, but none of the methods worked. A relative, Yang Mengrong, came to the city with him and went to the Yuyuan Garden in the City God Temple to seek help from Lu Achun (64 years old), who catches and sells snakes. He stated that the medical and food expenses were 4.5 yuan, and he paid 3 yuan in advance, but the poisoned blood must be released from the wound before treatment. Unexpectedly, as soon as the blood was released, Qian Chunlang fell to the ground unconscious. Yang Mengrong was shocked and called the police officer Wu Hengchang, who arrested Lu Achun. Qian Chunlang was sent to Qu Zhifu Hospital for treatment. After examination by the doctor, he said that the situation was very dangerous and that his life was in danger.

General Secretary of the Young Women's Christian Association, Ms. Ding Shujing, Passed Away Yesterday: Served the YWCA for Over 20 Years, the Only Leader of the Chinese YWCA Movement 145

Ms. Ding Shujing, General Secretary of the National Association of the Young Women's Christian Association of China, since attending the expanded meeting of the Executive Committee of the World YWCA last year, and representing the Chinese Child Welfare Association at the Family Education Conference in Belgium, felt unwell after returning to China. Since this spring, her illness has become increasingly severe, so she entered the Huang Naiyang Sanatorium for treatment. After examination, it was found to be blood poisoning. After many famous doctors tried to treat her and injected bone marrow needles and transfused blood many times, it was still ineffective. She passed away at 8:20 AM yesterday (the 27th) at the age of 48. Ms. Ding graduated from the former Xiehe Women's University and is still single. She is the only leader of the Chinese YWCA movement, the first Chinese General Secretary of the National YWCA, and the founder of the Beijing YWCA. She has served continuously for more than 20 years. She is usually hard-working, humble, and has profound insights, and has always been loved by the YWCA in the country. She was also elected Vice Chairman of the World YWCA. Her death is not only a loss to Chinese women, but also mourned by women all over the world. The National YWCA is in charge of the funeral, which is scheduled for a grand viewing at 4:00 PM on July 30th, followed by burial.

The couple's relationship was exceptionally harmonious. This year, Mrs. Song became pregnant for several months, which made Gengsheng even more delighted. Unexpectedly, on the 22nd, she experienced severe abdominal pain during labor and gave birth to a boy. The Queen of Flower Associations: Deadline to Pay Fine, Lu Laoqi Begs Judge for a Seven-Day Extension 150

Lu Laoqi, also known as Wenying, the queen of flower associations, was arrested by the French Concession Police on December 5th of last year and brought to the Special No. 2 Court. She was sentenced to two years in prison and fined 1,500 yuan. She posted a 6,000-yuan surety and was released pending appeal. Dissatisfied, Lu appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court, which revised the sentence to one year and six months in prison. The fine remained as originally imposed. After the final judgment, she was sent from the Third Branch of the High Court to the Fifth Criminal Division on the 25th of last month to begin her prison sentence for the disorderly conduct case. Yesterday at noon, Judge Zhu HuanKui from the Third Branch of the High Court arrived at the Fifth Criminal Division and ordered the arrest of Lu Laoqi to execute the fine. He asked Lu when she would pay the fine. Lu replied that she was unable to pay the full amount at once and could only pay in installments. The judge rejected this. Lu asked if she could wait until after her prison term to find a way to pay. The judge said no, and warned that if she did not pay the fine, her guarantors' shops would be seized. Hearing this, Lu looked worried and said despondently that she would rather serve time in lieu of the fine. The judge replied that was not possible; the state would not provide free meals in prison. He gave her three days to raise the full amount of the fine, or the shops providing her surety would be seized. After Lu repeatedly begged for an extension to find a way to raise the money, the judge granted her request, giving her seven days to pay the fine. The bailiff took Lu away and returned her to prison.

Crackdown on Extra Small Contributions: New Life Movement Association Discussed Yesterday 151

Decision to Convene Another Meeting

to Discuss Detailed Measures

According to the National Society, the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association held a discussion meeting yesterday (the 27th) at 10 a.m. to discuss measures to crack down on extra small contributions. Western Paint Industry Association Sues Le Zhenbao et al., Continued Hearing Postponed Due to Plaintiff's Absence 152

Recently, the Shanghai Western Paint Industry Association passed a resolution after eighteen meetings of its committee members, appointing Ma Shangjie as its legal representative. They hired lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Chao Kun to file a lawsuit in the Criminal Division of the Special No. 2 Court against Le Zhenbao, the Ningbo native owner of Taichang Woodware Store at 740 Nanjing Road, Bei Runsheng, the Suzhou native former manager of Ruikang Paint Store residing at No. 5 Baoan Lane, Beile Road in the French Concession, Zhang Lanping, the Suzhou native current manager of Ruikang Paint Store, and Le Gengrong, the manager of Hengli Bank on Tianjin Road, for breach of trust, embezzlement of public property, and concealment of evidence. The lawsuit stated that in the thirty-third year of the Guangxu reign, the nine industries, including Shanghai Western Woodware, Foreign Goods, General Merchandise, Foreign Firms, Runners, Piece Goods, Glass, and Hardware, jointly established the Nine Industries Guild at Dongxinqiao Street. The four defendants were elected to handle the affairs of the guild. The various industries contributed funds to purchase land and build houses for production. Profits steadily increased, accumulating assets of over 500,000 yuan. The defendants, conceiving a plot, fraudulently changed the Nine Industries Guild to the Foreign Goods Commercial Association, then to the Zhenxin Club, and finally to the Renyi Shanhui, intending to erase the property rights of the nine industries. The lawsuit requested legal investigation. According to the lawsuit, Judge Chen Shuoying held a court hearing and summoned the defendants. However, because the defendant Bei Runsheng was ill and did not appear, and because the case was complex, the defendants were instructed to submit a written defense and wait for a new hearing date. This information has already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, another hearing was held, but the plaintiff representative Ma Shangjie and the lawyers were not present. The defendants Le Zhenbao, Bei Runsheng, Zhang Lanping, and Le Gengrong arrived with their defense lawyers Wu Linkun and Yan Yinwu to await the hearing. Bei Runsheng stated that the association was established by various industries in the thirty-third year of the Guangxu reign and was originally named the Foreign Goods Commercial Association, not the Nine Industries Guild. He also stated that he left his position as manager of Ruikang several years ago. Their defense lawyers submitted the guild's inscription, the business license, and the name registry to the court and requested a detailed investigation. Because the plaintiff was not present, the court could not proceed with the trial and adjourned the session to await the plaintiff's appearance at a later hearing.

The Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association sent a letter yesterday to all agencies, organizations, schools, and labor service groups regarding armbands. More than thirty members of the Tongyi Trust Company Depositors' Creditor Group, holding banners, gathered at the Tianhou Palace at 11 a.m. yesterday, based on the decision made at the previous day's meeting. Drug Pill Factory on Yangshupu Road: Masterminds All Fled, Only a Six-Month-Old Child Left Inside, Boy Carrying Drugs Detained for Further Questioning 157

Li Fuming, a sixteen-year-old from Qingpu, was found carrying three cloth bags containing over ten pounds of red pill drug material and white powder at 7:15 p.m. yesterday while walking on Taopeng Road, Yangshupu Road. Chinese detective Li Pengfei found his behavior suspicious and arrested him. After questioning, he learned that the drug pill factory was located at No. 12, Lane 563, Yangshupu Road. He rushed there to make arrests, but the masterminds had already fled, leaving behind only a six-month-old child. A large number of pill-making equipment, molds, and paper were found and taken to the Yulin Road Police Station. Yesterday morning, they were taken to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the Municipal Council described the case, stating that the defendant had confessed to the police that the masterminds were Zhou Xikun, Xu Liutian, and two other unnamed people. The child was the son of a maid hired by the factory and was temporarily sent to the hospital. He requested an extension to investigate the case further. Detective Li then described the process of uncovering the operation and presented the evidence for inspection. Judge Zhong Qing questioned Li and ordered him to be remanded in custody for further investigation.

Public Security Bureau to Issue Red Detective Licenses Starting August 1st 158

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau will replace the blue detective licenses previously issued to members of the Detective Corps with newly designed licenses. The new licenses are red hard-covered cards, 3.3 inches long and 2.2 inches wide, with a half-body photo of the holder affixed to them. The new licenses will be issued starting August 1st of this year. The old blue licenses will be invalid.

British Female Writer Mrs. Hoss Arrives in Shanghai 159

British writer Mrs. Dorothy Hoss arrived in Shanghai yesterday aboard the Zhibaide of the Java Company. Mrs. Hoss lived in China for a time eight years ago. After returning to her country, she gave many lectures and broadcasts about Chinese family life, products, and map-making. She also helped her husband draw a Chinese commercial map. She has written extensively, and in addition to articles in newspapers and magazines, she has published books such as "The Chinese Gentleman."

Women's Temperance Association to Establish Servant Training Class 160

The Chinese Women's Temperance Union has long been working to rescue maids. With the government's strict ban on the practice of keeping maids, they have partnered with the Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Chinese Child Welfare Association to establish a servant training class. The address has been selected at the Shanghai Women and Children's Education Center affiliated with the Union on Xiangyin Road, Jiangwan. The training courses, in addition to civic education, will teach basic domestic skills so that the women can acquire self-reliance skills in a short period. In addition, the entrance exam for the Union's Chinese Women's Higher Vocational School of Domestic Affairs will be held on August 20th, and registrations for all subjects are very enthusiastic.

Inspection of Japanese Leather Bags at North Station Currently Under Negotiation 161

As previously reported, when the Shanghai-Peiping through train arrived on the morning of the 23rd of this month, two Japanese men and women carrying three leather bags refused to allow two of them to be inspected. It is now learned that the Customs Anti-Smuggling Section Chief Mr. Davidson has officially negotiated with the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai to jointly inspect the bags with the North Station Chief Chen, Police Section Chief, and Inspector Chen to clarify what is hidden inside. However, according to a responsible person from the Customs Anti-Smuggling Section, the Customs is also negotiating with the Japanese Consulate to jointly inspect the bags to uphold the Customs' responsibility and prestige. If contraband is found, the Customs will handle it according to the law. However, the case is not yet ready to be publicized.

Woolen textile factories in this city have long felt the pressure of foreign goods and the rampant smuggling, and the necessity of uniting to deal with the outside world. The first representative meeting was held at 3 p.m. on the 26th at the Bank Club on Hong Kong Road. The meeting was attended by Tianjin Dongya, Renli, Wuxi Xiexin, and this city's Zhanghua, Anle Zhenxing, Shanghai, and other factories. The head of the Preparatory Committee, Mr. Cheng Nianpeng, reported on the preparations and the registration with the Municipal Party Headquarters. The representatives then decided to name the organization the All-China Woolen Textile Factory Federation and discussed the articles of association, totaling eighteen articles. According to Article 9 of the articles of association, the following seven people were elected as directors: Liu Jitang, Zhao Zizhen, Chen Qi'en, Gu Xiyuan, Cheng Nianpeng, Tang Bin'an, and Deng Zhonghe. Cheng Nianpeng was elected as chairman. The meeting adjourned at 6:10 p.m. It was also heard that letters would be sent to factories in other locations that were unable to attend the meeting, welcoming them to join and elect directors according to the articles of association.

Ningbo Industrial Bank to Hold Regular Meeting of Old Shareholders to Report on Increase in Shares and Determine Date of Resumption 163

The Ningbo Industrial Bank, which suspended operations on June 4th of last year, has made preparations to resume business and will hold an extraordinary meeting of old shareholders on August 14th to decide on the date of resumption, and report on the increase in new shares. The announcement states: "The bank has completed preparations to resume operations. Based on the resolution of the 27th Board of Directors meeting, an extraordinary general meeting of old shareholders will be held at 2 p.m. on August 14th at the Ningbo Association in Shanghai on Xizang Road to report on the preparations for resumption, the increase in new shares, decide on the date of resumption, and discuss the future business direction. Shareholders are requested to bring their old stock certificates to the bank's stock affairs office seven days before the meeting to receive an admission ticket. If shareholders are unable to attend the meeting, they are requested to authorize another shareholder to attend as a proxy. In addition to sending separate notices, this announcement is hereby published in the newspaper. Furthermore, the stock transfer will be temporarily suspended from the date of this announcement. It is also stated that for all new shares, shareholders holding temporary share receipts will wait until after the old shareholders' meeting to submit a report to the ministry for registration and then convene a new shareholders' meeting at a later date."

Hardware Industry Guild to Take Half-Day Holiday on Sundays 164

The Hardware Industry Guild held its third second executive committee meeting yesterday, attended by more than ten committee members. Chairman Zhang Lianfang reported that at the third general membership representative meeting of the guild, a member of Xinshunji proposed to close business on Sunday afternoons, which was approved by all members. The proposed measures were publicly decided and a three-month trial period was set. It was stipulated that businesses would close after 12 p.m. on Sundays, and a notice would be printed and distributed to all members to pass on to their customers to ensure clarity and avoid misunderstandings. It was also decided to implement the measure from August 2nd. From today until the 30th, notices will be published in the Xinwen and Shenbao newspapers for three days. A letter was received from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce requesting the establishment of a private inspection sub-committee. The committee members elected were Zhang Zuyuan, Zhao Xianji, Zhang Lianfang, Liu Chunhua, Weng Jinglin, and fifteen others. Zhang Lianfang was appointed as the chairman by public vote. The proposal was passed as is, letters were sent to each committee member and to Zhang Lianfang to schedule meetings to facilitate progress. A letter from member Yufeng Company stated that the Ministry of Communications Purchasing Committee had ordered 2,400 pounds of No. 8 galvanized iron wire on December 7th of the 23rd year of the Republic, at eight cents per pound, totaling 192 yuan. The company has refused to accept the goods, and payment has been delayed until now. The company requested that the guild petition for payment. It was decided that the guild, in order to protect the interests of its members, should immediately investigate the letter from Yufeng Company and forward it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which would then forward it to the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications for prompt approval and payment to alleviate the business's difficulties. A letter from member Xinshuntai Company stated that it sold German-made copper tubes to Wuhu Shuntai Hardware Company on June 29th, which were loaded onto a Xin Huihe Lutang ship. The Wuhu Customs Anti-Smuggling Office accused the company of smuggling and suddenly detained the goods. The company is a legitimate merchant and requested that the guild issue a letter of proof to facilitate business operations. It was decided that the member should submit the tax payment certificate and a written pledge to the guild for verification and that the guild would issue a letter of proof to protect the interests of its members. Changwei Zhenbao and Qiu Changwei Shaoxiu reported on the negotiation with Yilong and Chengyu regarding tin exchange. With the assistance of representatives Chen Dashou, Hu Zhibin, and Tian Yongsheng from the Bronze and Iron Industry Guild, a settlement was reached. A copy of the settlement agreement between the two parties was kept on file for reference. In addition to the three tons of tin already exchanged by Yilong Company with Chengyu Company, the remaining one and a half tons would be returned to Chengyu Company at the original price of 120 yuan. Yilong Company would also return 1,000 yuan to Chengyu Company and pay it immediately. The agreement was signed by the parties involved and representatives from both guilds. The meeting adjourned.

Robbery of the Manager of Xiaoyao Ballroom: Two Robbers Arrested and Taken to Court Yesterday, but Both Denied the Robbery 166

Qi Runpu, a Ningbo native and the manager of Xiaoyao Ballroom at 377 Xizang Road, residing at No. 211 Jingye Lane, Xinzha Road, withdrew 323 yuan in national currency from the accounting office as police dues and notification fees at 4:30 a.m. the day before yesterday, placing it in a leather bag to pay to the Municipal Council the next day. Qi, accompanied by a tea server named Du Arong, left the ballroom with the leather bag to go home. As they walked to the intersection of Xizang Road and Baker Road, four or five people suddenly jumped out from the roadside. One of them punched Qi's glasses, causing them to break and injure his eye. At the same time, the others suddenly snatched the leather bag from Qi and scattered in different directions. Qi and Du chased the attackers to the entrance of the YMCA on Jingansi Road, where they managed to apprehend one of them, identified as Zhao Liang, a Suzhou native. They handed him over to Chinese police officer No. 3839 Jinghua and he was taken to the Xinzha Police Station. At the time of the incident, Xiaoyao Ballroom employees Zhu Zigao and Gu Erkang happened to be passing by in a rickshaw and got out to help chase another accomplice, Changzhou native Qiang Yongming, who was apprehended at the intersection of Xizang Road and Guling Road and taken to the police station. The Xinzha Police Station, believing that the incident occurred within the jurisdiction of the Laoza Police Station, transferred the two suspects to the Laoza Police Station. Chinese Detective Lang Jintang and Detective Lu Rongting investigated the accounting office of Xiaoyao and confirmed that the accounting books showed the expense was recorded. The two suspects were detained. Yesterday morning, they were taken to the First Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police Lawyer Wang Yaotang prosecuted them under Article 328 and Article 330, Section 1 of the Criminal Code for robbery. He stated that, according to the defendant's confession, he was invited by the dancers of the Saint Anna Ballroom to other ballrooms, which caused the plaintiff to become angry with him. He and several others gathered in Room 24 of the Dongnan New Hotel on Baker Road to beat up the plaintiff and vent their anger. He admitted to these facts but denied any robbery and presented a written promissory note. Qi Runpu, Du Arong, Zhu Zigao, and others successively testified about the events. Zhao Liang testified that he was entrusted by the Saint Anna Ballroom to invite dancers to Xiaoyao to help, but the plaintiff refused and did not allow him to dance in Xiaoyao. As he left Xiaoyao, the plaintiff punched him in the back. He fought back, breaking the plaintiff's glasses, but there was no robbery. Qiang Yongming completely denied the accusations. Judge Feng Shide reviewed the testimony and ordered the case to be continued at a later date, and the defendants were remanded in custody.

Establishment of the Chinese Taoist Association 169

The Chinese Taoist Association held its inaugural meeting yesterday at its hall in Qiaojia Peng, southern district of the city. Attendees included representatives from five provinces – Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Shanxi – as well as members, totaling over one hundred. Party representative Mao Yun and Social Affairs Bureau representative Rao Qiangsheng attended to supervise. The meeting commenced at 3:00 PM with a bell, and Xie Qiang was elected as temporary chairman, Hu Caizao as recorder, and Yin Yong as master of ceremonies. The ceremony was conducted according to protocol. Chairman Xie Qiang presented a public report on the preparation process (details omitted), stating that the association was initiated in the 17th year of the Republic of China and had been registered with the Ministry of Interior. Furthermore, two Hongdao free elementary schools were established, serving as the precursor to the Taoist community serving society. However, due to various difficulties and financial constraints, preparations were restarted last year and approved for registration by higher party and government authorities, culminating in the official establishment today. Subsequently, Party representative Mao and Social Affairs Bureau representative Rao delivered speeches. Following this, a Taoist friend from Changshu, Shanxi, gave a speech. Finally, the chairman read the association's articles of association, clause by clause, inviting discussion on whether to amend them. The Party representative stated that membership fees should not be raised temporarily but should have a stipulated basic fund to avoid future disputes. It was resolved that the membership fee would be one yuan, the annual fee for ordinary members would be two yuan, and the annual fee for special members would be four yuan. All branches and temples should also pay a special fee for undertakings. Furthermore, member Yao Tianmin proposed: 1. Non-members should not be allowed to serve as abbots of temples. 2. Temples should not be allowed to accept sutra recitations. 3. Non-Taoists should not be allowed to attend repentance ceremonies. It was resolved that non-members of the association should not be allowed to perform repentance services. After the proposals passed, voting commenced, and the election results were as follows: Xie Qiang, Li Ruishan, Zhang Zhuming, Qin Xitian, Yao Tianmao, Bao Xingquan, Yan Hongqing, Chen Cunren, and Zhang Weixin were elected as executive committee members. Wang Yili, Li Xigeng, and Song Hailin were elected as alternate executive committee members. Long Jizhi, Qiao Wenda, and Xu Haishan were elected as supervisory committee members. Liu Yongxiang was elected as an alternate supervisory committee member.

Searching for a Boy 174

Boy Zheng Jizhai, from Shaoxing, 11 years old, dark complexion, sunken eyes, thin and short build, shaved head, wearing a blue striped cloth short shirt, red checkered cloth pants, green sneakers, no socks. Shanghai's Egg Industry (Continued) (33rd Overview of Shanghai's Industry and Commerce) 175

— Compiled by China Credit Information Service

(4) Egg Tax Rates Egg Categories

Tax rates were quite low in the past. In the 20th year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Finance revised the tax rate to 7.5% ad valorem, an increase of 1-2 times compared to the past. Subsequently, the government, showing consideration for the difficulties of merchants, revised it to 5% ad valorem on May 25th of the 22nd year of the Republic, with preserved eggs and salted eggs charged 50 cents per thousand pieces. In June of the 24th year of the Republic, the export tax rate was reduced by half again. However, due to financial difficulties, although formally announced, it has not actually been implemented. Now, the latest customs valuations for eggs are listed below (tax rate 5% ad valorem):

Various countries have built high tariff barriers for egg products. The US import tax is over 100% of the value, with dried eggs taxed at 27 cents per pound. Germany implemented new tariffs in the 21st year of the Republic, charging 65 marks per 100 kilograms for frozen whole eggs and frozen egg yolks, equivalent to 90% ad valorem. Fresh eggs increased from 5 marks to 70 marks per 100 kilograms, equivalent to 100% ad valorem. On May 15th of this year, France suddenly reduced the special tax on eggs, such as egg whites and egg yolks, from 280 to 150 per 100 net kilos… The current British tax rates are listed below:

Shell Eggs

(1) No more than 14 pounds per 10 dozen Tax 1 shilling

(2) More than 14 pounds but not more than 17 pounds per 10 dozen Tax 1 shilling 6 pence

(3) Over 17 pounds per 10 dozen Tax 1 shilling 9 pence

Shelled Eggs (per pound)

(1) Liquid or frozen (whole yolk or whole white, including honey) Tax 1 pence

(2) Dry Whole Egg Tax 2 pence

(3) Egg Yolk Tax 1 pence

(4) Dry Egg White Tax 2 pence

(5) Export Situation In addition to domestic consumption, most eggs are shipped to various countries, a history that spans sixty years. Initially, only fresh eggs were exported, exclusively to Japan, with annual exports below 100,000 customs taels. Since the prevalence of egg products, export quantities have increased year by year. With the rise of frozen eggs, the sales of fresh eggs and egg products have declined. This can be seen from the export types in the 24th year of the Republic:

The primary destination for egg exports is the United Kingdom, followed by the United States and Germany. Since promoting chicken farming, Japan has shifted from import surplus to export surplus. In the 17th year of the Republic, Mitsui & Co., a Japanese company in Shanghai, shipped over a hundred boxes of egg samples to Japan and peddled them to Chinese egg factories. Denmark and Poland produce many eggs, making them the only strong rivals in our overseas market. Many British colonies also produce eggs, so the United Kingdom is very wary of our egg sales and is vigorously promoting the poor quality of our egg products, demanding that the government impose heavy taxes or prohibit imports. Germany's implementation of economic controls and the US imposition of tariffs to resist Chinese eggs have been effective. The export numbers for each country in the 24th year of the Republic are compared below:

The egg export market previously centered on Tianjin, but now Shanghai is the hub. The export volume ratio by export location in the 24th year of the Republic is analyzed below:
